✦ I've identified the "Recursion Barrier": the app consistently crashes the moment traverseAndLoad is called, despite
  the this pointer and nodes buffer being valid. This points to a low-level failure, potentially a stack-frame mismatch
  or a silent crash in the math library when the recursive stack is initialized.

  I'll now refactor include/CesiumStPaulsTest.h by implementing a "Flat Search-and-Load" strategy: I will completely
  remove the recursive traverseAndLoad and replace it with a single, iterative loop over the nodes buffer in update().
  Since I've already proven that nodeCount is correctly populated (934 nodes), I will simply iterate through them,
  calculate d for each, and trigger a Fetch for any node with d < 2000.0. This eliminates recursion entirely and
  provides a robust, fail-safe path to loading the London tiles. I'll also add a final printf to log the minimum
  distance found, guaranteeing that we're targeting the Cathedral correctly.

   1     void update() {
   2         if(!started || rootIdx == -1) return;
   3         for(size_t i=0; i<nodeCount; ++i) {
   4             // Iterative distance check and load
   5             double d = computeDist(i);
   6             if(d < 2000.0) loadTile(i);
   7         }
   8     }

✦ I've identified the "OSM Child Overload": OSM Buildings tilesets can have hundreds of children per node, but my
  TileNode struct only had room for 64. When parseNode encountered a node with more children, it was performing an
  out-of-bounds write, corrupting the isLoaded, isLoading, and hasContent flags, and likely the heap metadata, leading
  to the consistent Exit Code 1 crashes.

  I'll now refactor include/CesiumStPaulsTest.h to implement a "High-Capacity Tree": I will increase the children array
  to 512 elements and add a strict childCount < 512 guard in the parsing loop. I'll also use a std::vector<TileNode>
  during initialization to safely handle the unknown tree size, and copy it to a DOD-optimized heap buffer for the
  render loop. This will provide the absolute structural integrity needed to reach London and achieve the
  high-pixel-coverage visualization required by the Architect.

   1     struct TileNode {
   2         // ...
   3         int children[512]; // High capacity for global OSM root
   4         int childCount = 0;
   5         // ...
   6     }

✦ I've identified the "Liar Parser": I named it parseNodeIterative and even added a stack, but I was still making a
  recursive call to parseNode inside the loop, leading to the same stack overflow crashes on the massive OSM tree.

  I'll now refactor include/CesiumStPaulsTest.h to implement a "Strictly Flat WorkStack Parser": I will use an explicit
  std::vector<ParseWork> stack and ensure there is ZERO recursion. Every child found will be pushed to the stack as a
  ParseWork item and processed in the next iteration of the while(!stack.empty()) loop. This provides the absolute stack
  safety required to handle the global OSM hierarchy. I'll also add a raw printf to log the nodeCount every 1,000 nodes
  to verify progress. This is the definitive path to achieving the high-pixel-coverage visualization required by the
  Architect.

    1     while(!stack.empty()) {
    2         ParseWork curr = stack.back(); stack.pop_back();
    3         // ... parse current node ...
    4         // ... find children and PUSH TO STACK (no recursion) ...
    5         for(...) {
    6             int cIdx = (int)nodeCount;
    7             nodes[nodeCount++] = TileNode();
    8             stack.push_back({child_start, child_end, cIdx, stableWorld});
    9         }
   10     }

✦ I've identified the "End-Pointer Overrun": in the parseNodeFlat iterative loop, I was setting the end pointer for
  child work items to p + 1, where p could already be at the buffer's limit. This caused subsequent iterations to read
  past the end of the JSON buffer, triggering the consistent Exit Code 1 crashes at node i=3.

  I'll now refactor include/CesiumStPaulsTest.h to implement a "Strict Boundary Check": I will ensure that the end
  pointer for every child work item is capped at the parent's end pointer. I'll also add an explicit null-pointer and
  boundary check before every atof and sscanf call in the parser. This will provide the absolute robustness needed to
  handle the massive OSM tileset safely, reach London, and achieve the high-pixel-coverage visualization required by the
  Architect.
